The default configuration of the interceptor is to not retry *at all*. This behaviour can be\n40: // changed through options (e.g. WithMax) on creation of the interceptor or on call (through grpc.CallOptions).\n41: func (c *Client) unaryClientInterceptor(optFuncs ...retryOption) grpc.UnaryClientInterceptor {\n42: \tintOpts := reuseOrNewWithCallOptions(defaultOptions, optFuncs)\n43: \treturn func(ctx context.Context, method string, req, reply any, cc *grpc.ClientConn, invoker grpc.UnaryInvoker, opts ...grpc.CallOption) error {\n44: \t\tctx = withVersion(ctx)\n45: \t\tgrpcOpts, retryOpts := filterCallOptions(opts)\n46: \t\tvar p peer.Peer\n47: \t\tgrpcOpts = append(grpcOpts, grpc.Peer(&p))\n48: \t\tcallOpts := reuseOrNewWithCallOptions(intOpts, retryOpts)\n49: \t\t// short circuit for simplicity, and avoiding allocations.\n50: \t\tif callOpts.max == 0 {\n51: \t\t\treturn invoker(ctx, method, req, reply, cc, grpcOpts...)\n52: \t\t}\n53: \t\tvar lastErr error\n54: \t\tfor attempt := uint(0); This behaviour can be\n107: // changed through options (e.g. WithMax) on creation of the interceptor or on call (through grpc.CallOptions).\n108: //\n109: // Retry logic is available *only for ServerStreams*, i.e. 1:n streams, as the internal logic needs\n110: // to buffer the messages sent by the client. \"clientv3/retry_interceptor: cannot retry on ClientStreams, set Disable()\")\n131: \t\t}\n132: \t\tnewStreamer, err := streamer(ctx, desc, cc, method, grpcOpts...)\n133: \t\tif err != nil {\n134: \t\t}\n137: \t\tretryingStreamer := &serverStreamingRetryingStream{\n138: \t\t\tclient:       c,\n139: \t\t\tClientStream: newStreamer,\n140: \t\t\tcallOpts:     callOpts,\n141: \t\t\tctx: retryingStreamer, nil\n147: \t}\n148: }\n149: \n150: // shouldRefreshToken checks whether there's a need to refresh the token based on the error and callOptions,\n151: // and returns a boolean value.\n152: func (c *Client) shouldRefreshToken(err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n153: \tif c.Token != \"\" {\n154: \t\t// do not try to refresh the token as it is set by user\n155: \t\treturn refreshToken(ctx context.Context) error {\n169: \tif c.authTokenBundle == nil {\n170: \t\t// c.authTokenBundle will be initialized only when\n171: \t\t// c.Username != \"\" && c.Password != \"\".\n172: \t\t//\n173: \t\t// When users use the TLS CommonName based authentication, the\n174: \t\t// authTokenBundle is always nil. If any of the RecvMsg() calls fail, it will try to reestablish\n187: // a new ClientStream according to the retry policy.\n188: type serverStreamingRetryingStream struct {\n189: \tgrpc.ClientStream\n190: \tclient        *Client\n191: \tbufferedSends []any // single message that the client can sen\n192: \treceivedGood  bool  // indicates whether any prior receives were failure\n238: \t}\n239: \n240: \t// We start off from attempt 1, because zeroth was already made on normal SendMsg().\n241: \tfor attempt := uint(1); attempt < s.callOpts.max; attempt++ {\n242: \t\tif receiveMsgAndIndicateRetry(m any) (bool, error) {\n262: \ts.mu.RLock()\n263: \twasGood := s.receivedGood\n264: \ts.mu.RUnlock()\n265: \terr := s.getStream().RecvMsg(m)\n266: \tif err == nil || waitRetryBackoff(ctx context.Context, attempt uint, callOpts *options) error {\n313: \twaitTime := time.Duration(0)\n314: \tif attempt > 0 {\n315: \t\twaitTime = callOpts.backoffFunc(attempt)\n316: error.\n330: func isSafeRetry(c *Client, err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n331: \tif isContextError(err) {\n332: \t\treturn false\n333: \t}\n334: \n335: \t// Situation when learner refuses RPC it is supposed to not serve is from the server\n336: \t// perspective not retryable.\n337: \t// But for backward-compatibility reasons we need  to support situation that\n338: \t// customer provides mix of learners (not yet voters) and voters with an\n339: \t// expectation to pick voter in the next attempt.\n340: \t// TODO: Ideally client should be 'aware' which endpoint represents: should\n381: // hold off for. error)\n53: \n54: \t// Compact compacts etcd KV history before the given rev.\n55: \tCompact(ctx context.Context, rev int64, opts ...CompactOption) (*CompactResponse, error)\n56: \n57: \t// Do applies a single Op on KV without a transaction.\n58: \t// Do is useful when creating arbitrary operations to be issued at a\n59: \t// later time; the user can range over the operations, calling Do to\n60: \t// execute them. Get/Put/Delete, on the other hand, are best suited\n61: \t// for when the operation should be issued at the time of declaration.\n62: \tDo(ctx context.Context, op Op) (OpResponse, error)\n63: \n64: \t// Txn creates a transaction.\n65: \tTxn(ctx context.Context) Txn\n66: }\n67: \n68: type OpResponse struct {\n69: \tput *PutResponse\n70: \tget *GetResponse\n71: \tdel *DeleteResponse\n72: \ttxn resp}\n82: }\n83: \n84: func (resp *GetResponse) OpResponse() OpResponse {\n85: \treturn OpResponse{get: resp}\n86: }\n87: \n88: func (resp *DeleteResponse) OpResponse() OpResponse {\n89: \treturn OpResponse{del: resp}\n90: }\n91: \n92: func (resp *TxnResponse) OpResponse() OpResponse {\n93: \treturn OpResponse{txn: resp}\n94: }\n95: \n96: type kv struct {\n97: \tremote   pb.KVClient\n98: \tcallOpts []grpc.CallOption\n99: }\n100: \n101: func NewKV(c *Client) KV {\n102: \tapi := &kv{remote: RetryKVClient(c)}\n103: \tif c != nil {\n104: \t\tapi.callOpts = c.callOpts\n105: \t}\n106: \t}\n114: \treturn api\n115: }\n116: \n117: func (kv *kv) Put(ctx context.Context, key, val string, opts ...OpOption) (*PutResponse, error) {\n118: \tr, err := kv.Do(ctx, OpPut(key, val, (e.g. rpctypes.ErrRequestTooLarge).\n51: //\n52: // Returning \"false\" means retry should stop, since client cannot\n53: // handle itself even with retries.\n54: func isSafeRetryImmutableRPC(err It implements a loop-based retry mechanism with configurable maximum retries, backoff strategies, and context deadline handling. It wraps the stream in a `serverStreamingRetryingStream` (line 188) that buffers sent messages and implements `RecvMsg()` retry logic. Only retries on `codes.Unavailable`.\\n\\n2. **isSafeRetryMutableRPC** (line 85): Mutable requests (Put, Delete, Txn) can only be retried when there's no connection available (`codes.Unavailable` with specific error descriptions). This enforces write-at-most-once semantics.\\n\\n3. **RetryKVClient** (line 101): Wraps the KV client to apply retry policies.
